**Russia**,[^2] or the **Russian Federation**,[^3] [^4] is a country in [Eastern Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Europe "Eastern Europe") and [North Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Asia "North Asia"). It is the [largest country in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area "List of countries and dependencies by area"), spanning [eleven time zones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_in_Russia "Time in Russia") and sharing [land borders with fourteen countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borders_of_Russia "Borders of Russia").[^5] With a population of over 140 million, Russia is the [most populous country in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population "List of European countries by population") and the [ninth-most populous in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population"). It is a [highly urbanised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urbanization_by_sovereign_state "Urbanization by sovereign state") country, with sixteen of its urban areas having more than 1 million inhabitants. [Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow "Moscow"), the [most populous metropolitan area in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Europe "List of metropolitan areas in Europe"), is the capital and [largest city of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Russia_by_population "List of cities and towns in Russia by population"), while [Saint Petersburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg") is its second-largest city and [a major cultural centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society_and_culture_in_Saint_Petersburg "Society and culture in Saint Petersburg").

Human settlement on modern Russian territory dates back to the [Lower Paleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic "Lower Paleolithic"). The emergence of the [East Slavs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Slavs "East Slavs") as a prominent group in Europe between the 3rd and 8th centuries AD led to the establishment of [Kievan Rus'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27 "Kievan Rus'") in the 9th century, which adopted [Orthodox Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Eastern Orthodox Church") from the [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire") in 988. Following its disintegration, the late medieval [Grand Principality of Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Principality_of_Moscow "Grand Principality of Moscow") led the [unification of Russian lands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gathering_of_the_Russian_lands "Gathering of the Russian lands"), culminating in the formation of the [Tsardom of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia "Tsardom of Russia") in 1547. By the early 18th century, Russia had expanded vastly through [conquest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Siberia "Russian conquest of Siberia"), annexation, and the [efforts of Russian explorers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Russian_explorers "List of Russian explorers"). It was proclaimed as the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") in 1721, which became the [third-largest empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_empires "List of largest empires") in history. The [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution") of 1917 led to [the abolition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/February_Revolution "February Revolution") of the [Russian monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_monarchy "Russian monarchy") and the creation of the [Russian SFSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_SFSR "Russian SFSR"), the first [socialist state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_state "Socialist state"). Following the [Russian Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War "Russian Civil War"), Russia became the [largest and principal constituent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union "Republics of the Soviet Union") of the newly established [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") in 1922. Amidst [rapid industrialisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Industrialization in the Soviet Union") in the 1930s, [millions died](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excess_mortality_in_the_Soviet_Union_under_Joseph_Stalin "Excess mortality in the Soviet Union under Joseph Stalin") under [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"). The Soviet Union played [a decisive role](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union_in_World_War_II "Soviet Union in World War II") for the [Allies in World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") by leading large-scale efforts on the [Eastern Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_\(World_War_II\) "Eastern Front (World War II)"). During the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"), it emerged as a [superpower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower "Superpower") and competed with the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States") for [ideological dominance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ideological_dominance "Ideological dominance"). The Soviet era saw some of the most significant [Russian technological achievements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_Russian_innovation "Timeline of Russian innovation"), including the [first human-made satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sputnik_1 "Sputnik 1") and the [first human expedition into outer space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vostok_1 "Vostok 1").

In 1991, the Russian SFSR emerged from the [dissolution of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union") as the Russian Federation. Following [a constitutional crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993_Russian_constitutional_crisis "1993 Russian constitutional crisis") in 1993, [a new constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia "Constitution of Russia") was adopted, establishing a [semi-presidential republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-presidential_system "Semi-presidential system"). Since 1999, Russia's [political system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_Russia "Politics of Russia") has been dominated by [Vladimir Putin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin"), under [whose leadership](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_under_Vladimir_Putin "Russia under Vladimir Putin") it has experienced [democratic backsliding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_backsliding "Democratic backsliding"), transforming into an [authoritarian regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarianism "Authoritarianism"). Russia [has been militarily involved](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_history_of_the_Russian_Federation "Military history of the Russian Federation") in [numerous conflicts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Russia#Russian_Federation_\(1991%E2%80%93present\) "List of wars involving Russia"), including [its war with Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War "Russo-Georgian War") in 2008 and [its war with Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War "Russo-Ukrainian War") since 2014, which in the latter has involved the internationally unrecognised [annexation of Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Russian_annexation_of_Crimea "2014 Russian annexation of Crimea") in 2014 and [four additional regions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_annexation_of_Donetsk,_Kherson,_Luhansk_and_Zaporizhzhia_oblasts "Russian annexation of Donetsk, Kherson, Luhansk and Zaporizhzhia oblasts") following the [2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine"), resulting in a [full-scale war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_war_\(2022%E2%80%93present\) "Russo-Ukrainian war (2022–present)").

Russia is generally considered a [great power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_power "Great power") and [wields significant regional influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regional_power "Regional power") in Europe, [possessing the largest stockpile of nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Russia and weapons of mass destruction") and having the [third-highest military expenditure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures "List of countries by military expenditures") in the world. [Its economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Russia "Economy of Russia") ranks among the [largest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)"), relying on its [vast mineral and energy resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_as_an_energy_superpower "Russia as an energy superpower"), mainly [oil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_production "List of countries by oil production") and [natural gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_production "List of countries by natural gas production"). Russia continues to [rank very low](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_rankings_of_Russia "International rankings of Russia") in measurements of [democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy "Democracy"), [human rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Russia "Human rights in Russia") and [media freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_freedom_in_Russia "Media freedom in Russia"), while [having high levels of corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corruption_in_Russia "Corruption in Russia"). As the [successor state of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Succession_of_the_Soviet_Union "Succession of the Soviet Union"), it [retains its seat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union_and_the_United_Nations "Soviet Union and the United Nations") as a [permanent member of the United Nations Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council "Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council") and is a member state of [several international organisations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Russia#International_membership "Foreign relations of Russia"). Russia is also home to [32](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Russia "List of World Heritage Sites in Russia") UNESCO [World Heritage Sites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site").

## Etymology

According to the *[Oxford English Dictionary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary "Oxford English Dictionary")*, the English name *Russia* first appeared in the 14th century, borrowed from [Medieval Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin_language "Medieval Latin language"): *Russia*, used in the 11th century and frequently in 12th-century British sources, in turn derived from *Russi*, 'the Russians' and the suffix *[\-ia](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-ia#Latin "wikt:-ia")*.[^31] [^32]

There are several words in Russian which translate to "Russians" in English. The noun and adjective русский, *russkiy* refers to ethnic [Russians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russians "Russians"). The adjective российский, *rossiiskiy* denotes [Russian citizens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_citizenship_law "Russian citizenship law") regardless of ethnicity. The same applies to the more recently coined noun россиянин, *rossiianyn*, in the sense of citizen of the Russian state.[^33] [^34]

The oldest [endonyms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endonym_and_exonym "Endonym and exonym") used were *Rus'* (Русь) and the "Russian land" (Русская земля, *Russkaya zemlya*).[^35] According to the *[Primary Chronicle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_Chronicle "Primary Chronicle")*, the word *Rus'* is derived from the [Rus' people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rus%27_people "Rus' people"), who were a [Swedish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedes "Swedes") tribe, and from where the three original members of the [Rurikid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rurikid "Rurikid") dynasty came from.[^36] The [Finnish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finnish_language "Finnish language") word for Swedes, *ruotsi*, has the same origin.[^37] In modern historiography, the early medieval [East Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Slavs "East Slavs") state is usually referred to as *[Kievan Rus'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27 "Kievan Rus'")*, named after its capital city.[^38] Another Medieval Latin name for *Rus'* was *[Ruthenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruthenia "Ruthenia")*.[^39]

In Russian, the current name of the country, Россия (*Rossiya*), comes from the [Byzantine Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Greek "Byzantine Greek") name Ρωσία (*Rosía*).[^40] The name Росия (*Rosiya*) was first attested in 1387.[^41] The name *Rossiya* appeared in Russian sources in the 15th century and began to replace the vernacular *Rus'* during the rise of Moscow as the centre of a unified Russian state.[^42] However, until the end of the 17th century, the country was more often referred to by its inhabitants as *Rus'*, the "Russian land" (*Russkaya zemlya*), or the "Muscovite state" (*Moskovskoye gosudarstvo*), among other variations.[^43] [^33]

In 1721, [Peter the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_the_Great "Peter the Great") proclaimed the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") (*Rossiyskaya imperiya*).[^43] The name *Rossiya* was used as the common designation for the multinational Russian Empire and then for the modern Russian state.[^44] *Rossiya* is distinguished from the ethnonym *russkiy*, as it refers to a supranational identity, including ethnic Russians.[^44] After the [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution") and the proclamation of the [Russian SFSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic") in 1918, the "Russian" in the title of the state was *Rossiyskaya*, rather than *Russkaya*, as the former denoted a multinational state, while the latter had ethnic dimensions.[^45] In modern Russian, the name *Rus'* is still used in poetry or prose to refer to either the older Russia or an imagined essence of Russia.[^38]

## History

### Early history

The first human settlement on Russia dates back to the [Oldowan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oldowan "Oldowan") period in the early [Lower Paleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic "Lower Paleolithic"). About 2 million years ago, representatives of *[Homo erectus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_erectus "Homo erectus")* migrated to the [Taman Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taman_Peninsula "Taman Peninsula") in southern Russia.[^46] [Flint](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flint "Flint") tools, some 1.5 million years old, have been discovered in the [North Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Caucasus "North Caucasus").[^47] [Radiocarbon dated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radiocarbon_dated "Radiocarbon dated") specimens from [Denisova Cave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denisova_Cave "Denisova Cave") in the [Altai Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altai_Mountains "Altai Mountains") estimate the oldest [Denisovan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denisovan "Denisovan") specimen lived 195–122,700 years ago.[^48] Fossils of *[Denny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denny_\(hybrid_hominin\) "Denny (hybrid hominin)")*, an [archaic human](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaic_human "Archaic human") hybrid that was half [Neanderthal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal "Neanderthal") and half Denisovan, and lived some 90,000 years ago, was also found within the latter cave.[^49] Russia was home to some of the last surviving Neanderthals, from about 45,000 years ago, found in [Mezmaiskaya cave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mezmaiskaya_cave "Mezmaiskaya cave").[^50]

The first trace of an [early modern human](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ust%27-Ishim_man "Ust'-Ishim man") in Russia dates back to 45,000 years, in [Western Siberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Siberia "Western Siberia").[^51] The discovery of high concentration cultural remains of [anatomically modern humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human "Human"), from at least 40,000 years ago, was found at [Kostyonki–Borshchyovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kostyonki%E2%80%93Borshchyovo "Kostyonki–Borshchyovo"),[^52] and at [Sungir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sungir "Sungir"), dating back to 34,600 years ago—both in [western Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Russia "European Russia").[^53] Humans reached [Arctic Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far_North_\(Russia\) "Far North (Russia)") at least 40,000 years ago, in [Mamontovaya Kurya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamontovaya_Kurya "Mamontovaya Kurya").[^54] [Ancient North Eurasian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_North_Eurasian "Ancient North Eurasian") populations from Siberia genetically similar to [Mal'ta–Buret' culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mal%27ta%E2%80%93Buret%27_culture "Mal'ta–Buret' culture") and [Afontova Gora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afontova_Gora "Afontova Gora") were an important genetic contributor to [Ancient Native Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Beringian "Ancient Beringian") and [Eastern Hunter-Gatherers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Hunter-Gatherer "Eastern Hunter-Gatherer").[^55]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Yamnaya_Steppe_Pastoralists.jpg/330px-Yamnaya_Steppe_Pastoralists.jpg)

Bronze Age spread of Yamnaya Steppe pastoralist ancestry between 3300 and 1500 BC, 56 including the Afanasievo culture of southern Siberia

The [Kurgan hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurgan_hypothesis "Kurgan hypothesis") places the Volga-Dnieper region of southern Russia and [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") as the [urheimat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urheimat "Urheimat") of the [Proto-Indo-Europeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans "Proto-Indo-Europeans").[^57] Early [Indo-European migrations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_migrations "Indo-European migrations") from the [Pontic–Caspian steppe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pontic%E2%80%93Caspian_steppe "Pontic–Caspian steppe") of Ukraine and Russia spread [Yamnaya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yamnaya_culture "Yamnaya culture") ancestry and [Indo-European languages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages "Indo-European languages") across large parts of Eurasia.[^58] [^59] [Nomadic pastoralism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nomadic_pastoralism "Nomadic pastoralism") developed in the Pontic–Caspian steppe beginning in the [Chalcolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalcolithic "Chalcolithic").[^60] Remnants of these steppe civilisations were discovered in places such as [Ipatovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ipatovo_kurgan "Ipatovo kurgan"),[^60] [Sintashta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sintashta "Sintashta"),[^61] [Arkaim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arkaim "Arkaim"),[^62] and [Pazyryk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pazyryk_burials "Pazyryk burials"),[^63] which bear the earliest known traces of [horses in warfare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horses_in_warfare "Horses in warfare").[^61] The genetic makeup of speakers of the [Uralic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uralic_language_family "Uralic language family") language family in northern Europe was shaped by migration from [Siberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberia "Siberia") that began at least 3,500 years ago.[^64]

In the 3rd to 4th centuries AD, the [Gothic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goths "Goths") kingdom of [Oium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oium "Oium") existed in southern Russia, which was later overrun by [Huns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huns "Huns"). Between the 3rd and 6th centuries AD, the [Bosporan Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosporan_Kingdom "Bosporan Kingdom"), which was a Hellenistic [polity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polity "Polity") that succeeded the Greek colonies,[^65] was also overwhelmed by nomadic invasions led by warlike tribes such as the Huns and [Eurasian Avars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pannonian_Avars "Pannonian Avars").[^66] The [Khazars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khazars "Khazars"), who were of [Turkic origin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkic_peoples "Turkic peoples"), ruled the steppes between the Caucasus in the south, to the east past the Volga river basin, and west as far as [Kiev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiev "Kiev") on the Dnieper river until the 10th century.[^67] After them came the [Pechenegs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pechenegs "Pechenegs") who created a large confederacy, which was subsequently taken over by the [Cumans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cumans "Cumans") and the [Kipchaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kipchaks "Kipchaks").[^68]

The ancestors of [Russians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russians "Russians") are among the [Slavic tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_ancient_Slavic_peoples "List of ancient Slavic peoples") that separated from the Proto-Indo-Europeans, who appeared in the northeastern part of Europe c. 1500 years ago.[^69] The East Slavs gradually settled western Russia (approximately between modern [Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow "Moscow") and [Saint-Petersburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint-Petersburg "Saint-Petersburg")) in two waves: one moving from Kiev towards present-day [Suzdal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suzdal "Suzdal") and [Murom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murom "Murom") and another from [Polotsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polotsk "Polotsk") towards [Novgorod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novgorod "Novgorod") and [Rostov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rostov,_Yaroslavl_Oblast "Rostov, Yaroslavl Oblast").[^70] Prior to Slavic migration, that territory was populated by [Finno-Ugrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finno-Ugrian "Finno-Ugrian") peoples. From the 7th century onwards, the incoming East Slavs slowly assimilated the native Finno-Ugrians.[^71] [^72]

### Kievan Rus'

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Kievan-rus-1015-1113-%28en%29.png/250px-Kievan-rus-1015-1113-%28en%29.png)

Kievan Rus' after the Council of Liubech in 1097

The establishment of the first East Slavic states in the 9th century coincided with the arrival of the [Varangians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Varangians "Varangians"), [Vikings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vikings "Vikings") who ventured along the waterways extending from the eastern Baltic [to the Black](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/From_the_Varangians_to_the_Greeks "From the Varangians to the Greeks") and [Caspian Seas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga_trade_route "Volga trade route").[^73] [^74] According to the *[Primary Chronicle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_Chronicle "Primary Chronicle")*, a Varangian from the [Rus'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rus%27_people "Rus' people"), named [Rurik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rurik "Rurik"), was elected ruler of [Novgorod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novgorod "Novgorod") in 862.[^75] [^76] In 882, his successor [Oleg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oleg_of_Novgorod "Oleg of Novgorod") ventured south and conquered [Kiev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiev "Kiev"), which had been previously paying tribute to the [Khazars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khazars "Khazars").[^73] [^77] Rurik's son [Igor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Igor_of_Kiev "Igor of Kiev") and Igor's son [Sviatoslav](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sviatoslav_I_of_Kiev "Sviatoslav I of Kiev") subsequently subdued all local [East Slavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Slavs "East Slavs") tribes to Kievan rule, destroyed the Khazar state, and launched several military expeditions to [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sviatoslav%27s_invasion_of_Bulgaria "Sviatoslav's invasion of Bulgaria"), [Byzantium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paphlagonian_expedition_of_the_Rus%27 "Paphlagonian expedition of the Rus'") and [Persia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_expeditions_of_the_Rus%27 "Caspian expeditions of the Rus'").[^78] [^79] [^80]

During the 10th and 11th centuries, Kievan Rus' became one of the largest and most prosperous states in Europe. The reigns of [Vladimir the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_the_Great "Vladimir the Great") (980–1015) and his son [Yaroslav the Wise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yaroslav_the_Wise "Yaroslav the Wise") (1019–1054) constitute Kiev's [Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Age "Golden Age").[^81] Through his political and religious reforms, Vladimir laid the foundations for the transformation of Kievan Rus' from a fragmented conglomeration of tributary groups into a more unified realm, connected by dynastic authority and shared religious and cultural ties.[^82] He [adopted Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianisation_of_Kievan_Rus%27 "Christianisation of Kievan Rus'") from the [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"), beginning the synthesis of Byzantine and Slavic cultures that would define Russian culture for the next millennium.[^83] [^84] The reign of Yaroslav also saw the creation of the state's first written legal code, the *[Russkaya Pravda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russkaya_Pravda "Russkaya Pravda")*.[^85]

Kievan Rus' was politically unstable due to weak centralisation and the absence of a stable succession principle.[^86] The [rota system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rota_system "Rota system") introduced by Yaroslav led to princely authority being distributed among members of the ruling [Rurikid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rurikid "Rurikid") dynasty according to seniority.[^86] Intended to preserve dynastic unity, this system increasingly fostered rivalry among princes, leading to frequent infighting.[^86] [^87] As a result, political power fragmented among competing regional centres, marking a gradual shift toward decentralisation.[^87] [^88] [^89] Kiev's dominance waned, to the benefit of [Vladimir-Suzdal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal "Vladimir-Suzdal") in the north-east, the [Novgorod Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novgorod_Republic "Novgorod Republic") in the north, and [Galicia–Volhynia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galicia%E2%80%93Volhynia "Galicia–Volhynia") in the south-west.[^90] [^91] By the 12th century, Kiev lost its pre-eminence and Kievan Rus' had fragmented into different principalities.[^92] Prince [Andrey Bogolyubsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrey_Bogolyubsky "Andrey Bogolyubsky") sacked Kiev in 1169 and made [Vladimir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir,_Russia "Vladimir, Russia") his base,[^92] leading to political power being shifted to the north-east.[^90]

Vladimir-Suzdal continued the tradition of strong princely rule, while the Novgorod Republic, which formally won its independence in 1136, was an exception.[^93] From the mid-13th century, the throne of Novgorod was held by the grand princes of Vladimir, although the prince's authority gradually diminished in favour of more republican-style governance, with political power increasingly held by the *[veche](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veche "Veche")* (popular assembly) and elected officials.[^94] [^95]<sup><span title="Page / location: 83">: 83</span> </sup> Novgorod became a major commercial centre through the fur trade and an important centre of Russian culture.[^96] Led by Prince [Alexander Nevsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky "Alexander Nevsky"), the Novgorodians repelled the invading [Swedes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swedes "Swedes") in the [Battle of the Neva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Neva "Battle of the Neva") in 1240, as well as the [Germanic crusaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Crusades "Northern Crusades") in the [Battle on the Ice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_on_the_Ice "Battle on the Ice") in 1242.[^97] [^98]

Kievan Rus' finally fell to the [Mongol invasions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27 "Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'") of 1237–1240, which resulted in the [sacking of Kiev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Kiev_\(1240\) "Siege of Kiev (1240)") and other cities, as well as the death of a major part of the population.[^99] The invaders, later known as [Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatars "Tatars"), formed the state of the [Golden Horde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Horde "Golden Horde"), which ruled over Russia for the next two centuries.[^100] [^101] Only the Novgorod Republic escaped foreign occupation after it agreed to pay tribute to the Mongols.[^99] Galicia–Volhynia would later be absorbed by [Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania") and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_\(1025%E2%80%931385\) "Kingdom of Poland (1025–1385)"), while the Novgorod Republic continued to prosper in the north.[^90] In the northeast, the Byzantine-Slavic traditions of Kievan Rus' were adapted to form the Russian autocratic state.[^102]

### Grand Principality of Moscow

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg/250px-Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg)

Sergius of Radonezh blessing Dmitry Donskoy in Trinity Sergius Lavra, before the Battle of Kulikovo, depicted in a painting by Ernst Lissner

The destruction of Kievan Rus' saw the eventual rise of the [Grand Principality of Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Principality_of_Moscow "Grand Principality of Moscow"), initially a part of [Vladimir-Suzdal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal "Vladimir-Suzdal").[^71]<sup><span title="Pages: 11–20">: 11–20</span> </sup> While still under the domain of the [Mongol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol "Mongol") - [Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatars "Tatars") and with their connivance, Moscow began to assert its influence in the region in the early 14th century,[^103] gradually becoming the leading force in the "gathering of the Russian lands".[^104] [^105] When the seat of the metropolitan of the [Russian Orthodox Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church "Russian Orthodox Church") moved to Moscow in 1325, its influence increased.[^106] Moscow's last rival, the [Novgorod Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novgorod_Republic "Novgorod Republic"), prospered as the chief [fur trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fur_trade "Fur trade") centre and the easternmost port of the [Hanseatic League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hanseatic_League "Hanseatic League").[^107]

Led by Prince [Dmitry Donskoy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitry_Donskoy "Dmitry Donskoy") of Moscow, the united army of [Russian principalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_principalities "Russian principalities") inflicted [a milestone defeat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_conflicts_in_Eastern_Europe_during_Turco-Mongol_rule "List of conflicts in Eastern Europe during Turco-Mongol rule") on the Mongol-Tatars in the [Battle of Kulikovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Kulikovo "Battle of Kulikovo") in 1380.[^99] [^108] Moscow gradually absorbed its parent duchy and surrounding principalities, including formerly strong rivals such as [Tver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Principality_of_Tver "Principality of Tver") and [Novgorod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novgorod_Republic "Novgorod Republic").[^104]

[Ivan III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivan_III "Ivan III") ("the Great") threw off the control of the [Golden Horde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Horde "Golden Horde") and gained sovereignty over the ethnically Russian lands;[^109] he later adopted the title of [sovereign of all Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sovereign_of_all_Russia "Sovereign of all Russia").[^110] After the [fall of Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople "Fall of Constantinople") in 1453, Moscow [claimed succession to the legacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_Rome "Third Rome") of the [Eastern Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire "Eastern Roman Empire"). Ivan III married [Sophia Palaiologina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sophia_Palaiologina "Sophia Palaiologina"), the niece of the last [Byzantine emperor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_emperor "Byzantine emperor") [Constantine XI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_XI "Constantine XI"), and made the Byzantine [double-headed eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double-headed_eagle "Double-headed eagle") his own, and eventually Russia's, coat-of-arms.[^109] [Vasili III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vasili_III_of_Russia "Vasili III of Russia") united all of Russia by annexing the last few independent [Russian states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_tribes_and_states_in_Belarus,_Russia_and_Ukraine "List of tribes and states in Belarus, Russia and Ukraine") in the early 16th century.[^111]

### Tsardom of Russia

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Ivan_grozny_frame.jpg/250px-Ivan_grozny_frame.jpg)

Ivan IV was the Grand Prince of Moscow from 1533 to 1547, then Tsar of Russia until his death in 1584.

In development of the [Third Rome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow,_third_Rome "Moscow, third Rome") ideas, the grand prince [Ivan IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivan_IV "Ivan IV") ("the Terrible") was officially crowned as the first [tsar of all Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsar_of_all_Russia "Tsar of all Russia") in 1547. The tsar [promulgated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Promulgation "Promulgation") a new code of laws ([Sudebnik of 1550](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudebnik_of_1550 "Sudebnik of 1550")), established the first Russian feudal representative body (the [Zemsky Sobor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zemsky_Sobor "Zemsky Sobor")), revamped the military, curbed the influence of the clergy, and reorganised local government.[^71] During his long reign, Ivan nearly doubled the already large Russian territory by annexing the three Tatar khanates: [Kazan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khanate_of_Kazan "Khanate of Kazan") and [Astrakhan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astrakhan_Khanate "Astrakhan Khanate") along the [Volga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga "Volga"),[^112] and the [Khanate of Sibir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khanate_of_Sibir "Khanate of Sibir") in southwestern Siberia. Ultimately, by the end of the 16th century, Russia expanded east of the [Ural Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ural_Mountains "Ural Mountains").[^113] However, the Tsardom was weakened by the long and unsuccessful [Livonian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Livonian_War "Livonian War") against the coalition of the [Kingdom of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland "Crown of the Kingdom of Poland") and the [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania") (later the united [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth")), the [Kingdom of Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Sweden_\(1523%E2%80%931611\) "History of Sweden (1523–1611)"), and [Denmark–Norway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway "Denmark–Norway") for access to the Baltic coast and sea trade.[^114] In 1571, the [Crimean Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Khanate "Crimean Khanate"), supported by the [Ottomans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"), [burned down Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fire_of_Moscow_\(1571\) "Fire of Moscow (1571)"), destroying everything except the Kremlin. The following year, the Crimeans attempted another raid on Moscow, but this time they were defeated in the crucial [Battle of Molodi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Molodi "Battle of Molodi").[^115]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Fedor_chertezh.jpeg/250px-Fedor_chertezh.jpeg)

Feodor Godunov's map of Russia, as published by Hessel Gerritsz in 1614

The death of Ivan's sons marked the end of the ancient [Rurik dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rurik_dynasty "Rurik dynasty") in 1598, and in combination with the [famine of 1601–1603](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1601%E2%80%9303 "Russian famine of 1601–03"), led to a civil war, the rule of pretenders, and foreign intervention during the [Time of Troubles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_of_Troubles "Time of Troubles") in the early 17th century.[^116] The [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth"), taking advantage, occupied parts of Russia, extending into the capital Moscow.[^117] In 1612, the Poles were forced to retreat by the Russian volunteer corps, led by merchant [Kuzma Minin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuzma_Minin "Kuzma Minin") and prince [Dmitry Pozharsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitry_Pozharsky "Dmitry Pozharsky").[^118] The [Romanov dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanov_dynasty "Romanov dynasty") acceded to the throne in 1613 by the decision of the Zemsky Sobor, and the country started its gradual recovery from the crisis.[^119]

Russia continued its territorial growth through the 17th century, which was the age of the [Cossacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cossacks "Cossacks").[^120] In 1654, the Ukrainian leader, [Bohdan Khmelnytsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bohdan_Khmelnytsky "Bohdan Khmelnytsky"), offered to place Ukraine under the protection of the Russian tsar, [Alexis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexis_of_Russia "Alexis of Russia"), whose acceptance of this offer led to another [Russo-Polish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Polish_War_\(1654%E2%80%931667\) "Russo-Polish War (1654–1667)"). Ultimately, Ukraine was split along the [Dnieper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dnieper "Dnieper"), placing [Left-bank Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-bank_Ukraine "Left-bank Ukraine") and [Kiev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kiev "Kiev") under Russian rule.[^121] In the east, the rapid Russian exploration and colonisation of vast Siberia continued, hunting for valuable furs and ivory. [Russian explorers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Russian_explorers "List of Russian explorers") pushed eastward primarily along the [Siberian River Routes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberian_River_Routes "Siberian River Routes"), and by the mid-17th century, there were Russian settlements in eastern Siberia, on the [Chukchi Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula "Chukchi Peninsula"), along the [Amur River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amur_River "Amur River"), and on the coast of the Pacific Ocean.[^120] In 1648, [Semyon Dezhnyov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov "Semyon Dezhnyov") became the first European to navigate through the [Bering Strait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bering_Strait "Bering Strait").[^122]

### Imperial Russia

Under [Peter the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_the_Great "Peter the Great"), Russia was proclaimed an empire in 1721, and established itself as one of the European great powers. Ruling from 1682 to 1725, Peter defeated Sweden in the [Great Northern War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Northern_War "Great Northern War") (1700–1721), securing Russia's access to the sea and sea trade. In 1703, Peter founded [Saint Petersburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Petersburg "Saint Petersburg") on the Baltic Sea by establishing the [Peter and Paul Fortress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Fortress "Peter and Paul Fortress") as a strategic outpost; the city later replaced Moscow as Russia's capital in 1712. Throughout his rule, [sweeping reforms were made](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_reform_of_Peter_the_Great "Government reform of Peter the Great"), which brought significant Western European cultural influences to Russia.[^71] He was succeeded by [Catherine I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catherine_I_of_Russia "Catherine I of Russia") (1725–1727), followed by [Peter II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_II_of_Russia "Peter II of Russia") (1727–1730), and [Anna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anna_of_Russia "Anna of Russia"). The reign of Peter I's daughter [Elizabeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Russia "Elizabeth of Russia") from 1741 to 1762 saw Russia's participation in the [Seven Years' War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War "Seven Years' War") (1756–1763). During the conflict, Russian troops overran [East Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Prussia "East Prussia"), reaching Berlin.[^123] However, upon Elizabeth's death, all these conquests were returned to the [Kingdom of Prussia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia "Kingdom of Prussia") by pro-Prussian [Peter III of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_III_of_Russia "Peter III of Russia").[^124]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Growth_of_Russia_1547-1725.png/500px-Growth_of_Russia_1547-1725.png)

Expansion and territorial evolution of Russia from the coronation of Ivan IV to the death of Peter I

[Catherine II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catherine_the_Great "Catherine the Great") ("the Great"), who ruled from 1762 to 1796, presided over the [Russian Age of Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Enlightenment "Russian Enlightenment"). She extended Russian political control over the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth and [annexed most of its territories into Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland "Partitions of Poland"), making it the most populous country in Europe.[^125] In the south, after the successful [Russo-Turkish Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_Wars "Russo-Turkish Wars") against the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"), Catherine advanced Russia's boundary to the Black Sea, by dissolving the [Crimean Khanate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Khanate "Crimean Khanate"), and [annexing Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Empire "Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Empire").[^126] As a result of victories over [Qajar Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qajar_dynasty "Qajar dynasty") through the [Russo-Persian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars "Russo-Persian Wars"), by the first half of the 19th century, Russia also [conquered the Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_the_Caucasus "Russian conquest of the Caucasus").[^127] Catherine's successor, her son [Paul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia "Paul I of Russia"), was [unstable and focused predominantly on domestic issues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personality_and_reputation_of_Paul_I_of_Russia "Personality and reputation of Paul I of Russia").[^128] Following his short reign, Catherine's strategy was continued with [Alexander I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia "Alexander I of Russia") 's (1801–1825) [wresting of Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finnish_War "Finnish War") from the weakened Sweden in 1809,[^129] and of [Bessarabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bessarabia "Bessarabia") from the Ottomans in 1812.[^130] In North America, the Russians became the first Europeans to [reach and colonise Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_America "Russian America").[^131] In 1803–1806, the [first Russian circumnavigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation "First Russian circumnavigation") was made.[^132] In 1820, [a Russian expedition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fabian_Gottlieb_von_Bellingshausen#First_Russian_Antarctic_expedition "Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen") discovered the continent of [Antarctica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctica "Antarctica").[^133]

#### Great power and development of society, sciences, and arts

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Napoleons_retreat_from_Moscow_by_Adolph_Northen.jpg/250px-Napoleons_retreat_from_Moscow_by_Adolph_Northen.jpg)

Napoleon 's retreat from Moscow by Albrecht Adam (1851)

During the [Napoleonic Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars "Napoleonic Wars"), Russia joined alliances with various European powers, and fought against France. The [French invasion of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia "French invasion of Russia") at the height of Napoleon's power in 1812 reached Moscow, but eventually failed as the obstinate resistance in combination with the bitterly cold [Russian winter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_winter "Russian winter") led to a disastrous defeat of invaders, in which the pan-European [Grande Armée](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e "Grande Armée") faced utter destruction. Led by [Mikhail Kutuzov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Kutuzov "Mikhail Kutuzov") and [Michael Andreas Barclay de Tolly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Andreas_Barclay_de_Tolly "Michael Andreas Barclay de Tolly"), the [Imperial Russian Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army "Imperial Russian Army") ousted Napoleon and drove throughout Europe in the [War of the Sixth Coalition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition "War of the Sixth Coalition"), ultimately entering Paris.[^134] [Alexander I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia "Alexander I of Russia") controlled Russia's delegation at the [Congress of Vienna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna "Congress of Vienna"), which defined the map of post-Napoleonic Europe.[^135]

The officers who pursued Napoleon into Western Europe brought ideas of liberalism back to Russia, and attempted to curtail the tsar's powers during the abortive [Decembrist revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decembrist_revolt "Decembrist revolt") of 1825.[^136] At the end of the conservative reign of [Nicholas I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia "Nicholas I of Russia") (1825–1855), a zenith period of Russia's power and influence in Europe, was disrupted by defeat in the [Crimean War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_War "Crimean War").[^137]

#### Great liberal reforms and capitalism

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG/250px-The_defeat_of_Shipka_Peak%2C_Bulgarian_War_of_Independence.JPG)

The Battle of Shipka Pass for the control of the vital Shipka Pass during the 1877–1878 Russo-Turkish War

Nicholas's successor [Alexander II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia "Alexander II of Russia") (1855–1881) enacted significant changes throughout the country, including the [emancipation reform of 1861](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emancipation_reform_of_1861 "Emancipation reform of 1861").[^138] These reforms spurred industrialisation, and modernised the Imperial Russian Army, which liberated much of the [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans "Balkans") from Ottoman rule in the aftermath of the [1877–1878 Russo-Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_\(1877%E2%80%931878\) "Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)").[^139] During most of the 19th and early 20th centuries, Russia and [Britain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") colluded over [Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Afghanistan "Emirate of Afghanistan") and its neighbouring territories in [Central](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia") and South Asia; the rivalry between the two major European empires came to be known as the [Great Game](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Game "Great Game").[^140]

The late 19th century saw the rise of various socialist movements in Russia. Alexander II was [assassinated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Alexander_II_of_Russia "Assassination of Alexander II of Russia") in 1881 by revolutionary terrorists.[^141] The reign of his son [Alexander III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Russia "Alexander III of Russia") (1881–1894) was less liberal but more peaceful.[^142]

#### Constitutional monarchy and World War

During the reign of the last Russian emperor, [Nicholas II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_II "Nicholas II") (1894–1917), the [Revolution of 1905](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolution_of_1905 "Revolution of 1905") was precipitated by the disastrous and humiliating defeat in the [Russo-Japanese War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War "Russo-Japanese War").[^143] The uprising was put down, but the government was forced to concede major reforms ([Russian Constitution of 1906](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1906 "Russian Constitution of 1906")), including granting [freedoms of speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_speech "Freedom of speech") and [assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly "Freedom of assembly"), the legalisation of political parties, and the creation of an elected legislative body, the [State Duma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Duma_\(Russian_Empire\) "State Duma (Russian Empire)").[^144]

### Revolution and civil war

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg/250px-Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg)

Emperor Nicholas II of Russia and the Romanovs were executed by the Bolsheviks in 1918.

In 1914, [Russia entered World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_entry_into_World_War_I "Russian entry into World War I") in response to [Austria-Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria-Hungary "Austria-Hungary") 's declaration of war on Russia's ally [Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia "Kingdom of Serbia"),[^145] and fought across multiple fronts while isolated from its [Triple Entente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple_Entente "Triple Entente") allies.[^146] In 1916, the [Brusilov Offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brusilov_Offensive "Brusilov Offensive") of the Imperial Russian Army almost completely destroyed the [Austro-Hungarian Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Army "Austro-Hungarian Army").[^147] However, the already-existing public distrust of the regime was deepened by the rising costs of war, [high casualties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I_casualties "World War I casualties"), and rumours of corruption and treason. All this formed the climate for the [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution") of 1917, carried out in two major acts.[^71] In early 1917, [Nicholas II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia "Nicholas II of Russia") was [forced to abdicate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/February_Revolution "February Revolution"); he and his family were imprisoned and [later executed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shooting_of_the_Romanov_family "Shooting of the Romanov family") during the [Russian Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War "Russian Civil War").[^148] The monarchy was replaced by a shaky coalition of political parties that declared itself the [Provisional Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government "Russian Provisional Government"),[^149] and proclaimed the [Russian Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Republic "Russian Republic"). On 19 January \[[O.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates "Old Style and New Style dates") 6 January\], 1918, the [Russian Constituent Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Constituent_Assembly "Russian Constituent Assembly") declared Russia a democratic federal republic (thus ratifying the Provisional Government's decision). The next day the Constituent Assembly was dissolved by the [All-Russian Central Executive Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-Russian_Central_Executive_Committee "All-Russian Central Executive Committee").[^71]

An alternative socialist establishment co-existed, the [Petrograd Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrograd_Soviet "Petrograd Soviet"), wielding power through the democratically elected councils of workers and peasants, called *[soviets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_\(council\) "Soviet (council)")*. The rule of the new authorities only aggravated the crisis in the country instead of resolving it, and eventually, the [October Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution"), led by [Bolshevik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshevik "Bolshevik") leader [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin"), overthrew the Provisional Government and gave full governing power to the soviets, leading to the creation of the world's first [socialist state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_state "Socialist state").[^71] The [Russian Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Civil_War "Russian Civil War") broke out between the [anti-communist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communist "Anti-communist") [White movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_movement "White movement") and the Bolsheviks with its [Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army").[^150] In the aftermath of signing the [Treaty of Brest-Litovsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk "Treaty of Brest-Litovsk") that concluded hostilities with the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers") of [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), Bolshevist Russia surrendered most of its western territories, which hosted 34% of its population, 54% of its industries, 32% of its agricultural land, and roughly 90% of its coal mines.[^151]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Vladimir_Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.jpg/250px-Vladimir_Lenin_Speech_in_May_1920.jpg)

Vladimir Lenin speaks in Moscow, 1920, with Leon Trotsky leaning against the podium.

The [Allied powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I") launched an unsuccessful [military intervention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allied_intervention_in_the_Russian_Civil_War "Allied intervention in the Russian Civil War") in support of anti-communist forces.[^152] In the meantime, both the Bolsheviks and White movement carried out campaigns of deportations and executions against each other, known respectively as the [Red Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Terror "Red Terror") and [White Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Terror_\(Russia\) "White Terror (Russia)").[^153] By the end of the violent civil war, Russia's economy and infrastructure were heavily damaged, and as many as 10 million perished during the war, mostly civilians.[^154] Millions became [White émigrés](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_%C3%A9migr%C3%A9 "White émigré"),[^155] and the [Russian famine of 1921–1922](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1921%E2%80%931922 "Russian famine of 1921–1922") claimed up to five million victims.[^156]

### Soviet Union

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Russian_SFSR_in_Soviet_Union_%281936%29.svg/250px-Russian_SFSR_in_Soviet_Union_%281936%29.svg.png)

Location of the Russian SFSR (red) within the Soviet Union in 1936

#### Command economy and Soviet society

On 30 December 1922, Lenin and his aides [formed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Creation_of_the_USSR "Treaty on the Creation of the USSR") the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"), by joining the [Russian SFSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic") into a single state with the [Byelorussian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic"), [Transcaucasian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcaucasian_Socialist_Federative_Soviet_Republic "Transcaucasian Socialist Federative Soviet Republic"), and [Ukrainian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic") republics.[^157] Eventually, internal border changes and annexations during World War II resulted in a union of [15 republics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union "Republics of the Soviet Union"), the largest and most populous being the Russian SFSR, which dominated the union politically, culturally, and economically.[^158]

Following [Lenin's death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Vladimir_Lenin "Death and state funeral of Vladimir Lenin") in 1924, a [troika](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Troikas_in_the_Soviet_Union "List of Troikas in the Soviet Union") was designated to take charge. Eventually [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin"), the [General Secretary of the Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"), managed to suppress all opposition factions and consolidate power in his hands to become the country's dictator by the 1930s.[^159] [Leon Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky "Leon Trotsky"), the main proponent of [world revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_revolution "World revolution"), was exiled from the Soviet Union in 1929,[^160] and Stalin's idea of [Socialism in One Country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism_in_One_Country "Socialism in One Country") became the official line.[^161] The continued internal struggle in the Bolshevik party culminated in the [Great Purge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Purge "Great Purge").[^162]

#### Stalinism and modernisation

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Telegram_Stalin_STZ.jpg/250px-Telegram_Stalin_STZ.jpg)

Congratulations sent by Joseph Stalin on the opening of the Stalingrad Tractor Plant

Under Stalin's leadership, the government launched a [command economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Command_economy "Command economy"), [industrialisation of the largely rural country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_USSR "Industrialization in the USSR"), and [collectivisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_USSR "Collectivization in the USSR") of [its agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture_in_the_USSR "Agriculture in the USSR"). During this period of rapid economic and social change, millions of people were sent to [penal labour camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag "Gulag"), including many political convicts for their suspected or real opposition to Stalin's rule,[^163] and millions were [deported and exiled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union "Population transfer in the Soviet Union") to remote areas of the Soviet Union.[^164] The transitional disorganisation of the country's agriculture, combined with the harsh state policies and a drought,[^165] led to the [Soviet famine of 1932–1933](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1932%E2%80%931933 "Soviet famine of 1932–1933"), which killed 5.7 [^166] to 8.7 million, 3.3 million of them in the Russian SFSR.[^167] The Soviet Union, ultimately, made the costly transformation from a largely agrarian economy to a major industrial powerhouse within a short span of time.[^168]

#### World War II and United Nations

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9._%D0%98%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B8%D0%BC_30_%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82.jpg/250px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9._%D0%98%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B8%D0%BC_30_%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82.jpg)

Two teenage girls assemble PPD-40 submachine guns during the Siege of Leningrad in 1942.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/RIAN_archive_602161_Center_of_Stalingrad_after_liberation.jpg/250px-RIAN_archive_602161_Center_of_Stalingrad_after_liberation.jpg)

The Battle of Stalingrad, the largest and bloodiest battle in the history of warfare, ended in 1943 with a decisive Soviet victory against the German army.

The Soviet Union entered [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II") on 17 September 1939 with its [invasion of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland "Soviet invasion of Poland"),[^169] in accordance with a secret protocol within the [Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact "Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact") with [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany").[^170] The Soviet Union later [invaded Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winter_War "Winter War"),[^171] and [occupied and annexed the Baltic states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_\(1940\) "Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)"),[^172] as well as [parts of Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina "Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina").[^173]<sup><span title="Page / location: 91–95">: 91–95</span> </sup> On 22 June 1941, Germany [invaded the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa"),[^174] opening the [Eastern Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Front_\(World_War_II\) "Eastern Front (World War II)"), the largest theatre of World War II.[^175]<sup><span title="Page / location: 7">: 7</span></sup>

Eventually, some 5 million [Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") troops were captured by the Nazis;[^176]<sup><span title="Page / location: 272">: 272</span> </sup> the latter deliberately [starved to death or otherwise killed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war "German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war") 3.3 million Soviet [POWs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prisoner_of_war "Prisoner of war"), and a vast number of civilians, as the " [Hunger Plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunger_Plan "Hunger Plan") " sought to fulfil [Generalplan Ost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generalplan_Ost "Generalplan Ost").[^177]<sup><span title="Page / location: 175–186">: 175–186</span> </sup> Although the [Wehrmacht](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wehrmacht "Wehrmacht") had considerable early success, their attack was halted in the [Battle of Moscow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Moscow "Battle of Moscow").[^178] Subsequently, the Germans were dealt major defeats first at the [Battle of Stalingrad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad "Battle of Stalingrad") in the winter of 1942–1943,[^179] and then in the [Battle of Kursk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk "Battle of Kursk") in the summer of 1943.[^180] Another German failure was the [Siege of Leningrad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad "Siege of Leningrad"), in which the city was fully blockaded on land between 1941 and 1944 by German and Finnish forces, and suffered starvation and more than a million deaths, but never surrendered.[^181] Soviet forces steamrolled through Eastern and Central Europe in 1944–1945 and [captured Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin "Battle of Berlin") in May 1945.[^182] In August 1945, the Red Army [invaded Manchuria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria "Soviet invasion of Manchuria") and [ousted the Japanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_War "Soviet–Japanese War") from Northeast Asia, contributing to the Allied victory over Japan.[^183]

The 1941–1945 period of World War II is known in Russia as the [Great Patriotic War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Patriotic_War_\(term\) "Great Patriotic War (term)").[^184] The Soviet Union, along with the United States, the United Kingdom and China were considered the Big Four of Allied powers in World War II, and later became the [Four Policemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_Policemen "Four Policemen"), which was the foundation of the [United Nations Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council "United Nations Security Council").[^185]<sup><span title="Page / location: 27">: 27</span> </sup> During the war, [Soviet civilian and military death were about 26–27 million](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union "World War II casualties of the Soviet Union"),[^186] accounting for about half of all [World War II casualties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_casualties "World War II casualties").[^187]<sup><span title="Page / location: 295">: 295</span> </sup> The [Soviet economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union "Economy of the Soviet Union") and infrastructure suffered massive devastation, which caused the [Soviet famine of 1946–1947](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1946%E2%80%931947 "Soviet famine of 1946–1947").[^188] However, at the expense of a large sacrifice, the Soviet Union emerged as a superpower.[^189]

#### Superpower and Cold War

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/250px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg)

The " Big Three " at the Yalta Conference in February 1945, Winston Churchill, Franklin D. Roosevelt and Joseph Stalin

After World War II, according to the [Potsdam Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potsdam_Conference "Potsdam Conference"), the [Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army") occupied parts of Eastern and Central Europe, including [East Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") and the eastern regions of [Austria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria "Austria").[^190] Dependent communist governments were installed in the [Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") satellite states.[^191] After becoming the world's second [nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Russia and weapons of mass destruction"),[^192] the Soviet Union established the [Warsaw Pact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warsaw_Pact "Warsaw Pact") alliance,[^193] and entered into a struggle for global dominance, known as the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"), with the rivalling United States and [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO").[^194]

#### Khrushchev Thaw reforms and economic development

After [Stalin's death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Joseph_Stalin "Death and state funeral of Joseph Stalin") in 1953 and a short period of [collective leadership](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_leadership_in_the_Soviet_Union "Collective leadership in the Soviet Union"), the new leader [Nikita Khrushchev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev "Nikita Khrushchev") denounced [Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On_the_Cult_of_Personality_and_Its_Consequences "On the Cult of Personality and Its Consequences") and launched the policy of [de-Stalinization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De-Stalinization "De-Stalinization"), releasing many political prisoners from the [Gulag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag "Gulag") labour camps.[^195] The general easement of repressive policies became known later as the [Khrushchev Thaw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khrushchev_Thaw "Khrushchev Thaw").[^196] At the same time, Cold War tensions reached its peak when the two rivals clashed over the deployment of the United States [Jupiter missiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PGM-19_Jupiter "PGM-19 Jupiter") in Turkey and Soviet [missiles in Cuba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis "Cuban Missile Crisis").[^197]

In 1957, the Soviet Union launched the world's first artificial [satellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite "Satellite"), *[Sputnik 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sputnik_1 "Sputnik 1")*, thus starting the [Space Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Age "Space Age").[^198] Russian [cosmonaut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmonaut "Cosmonaut") [Yuri Gagarin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin "Yuri Gagarin") became the first human to orbit the Earth, aboard the *[Vostok 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vostok_1 "Vostok 1")* crewed spacecraft on [12 April 1961](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmonautics_Day "Cosmonautics Day").[^199]

#### Period of developed socialism or Era of Stagnation

Following the ousting of Khrushchev in 1964, another period of collective leadership ensued, until [Leonid Brezhnev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev "Leonid Brezhnev") became the leader. The era of the 1970s and the early 1980s was later designated as the [Era of Stagnation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation "Era of Stagnation"). The 1965 [Kosygin reform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosygin_reform "Kosygin reform") aimed for partial [decentralisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decentralisation "Decentralisation") of the [Soviet economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_economy "Soviet economy").[^200] In 1979, after a [communist-led revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saur_Revolution "Saur Revolution") in Afghanistan, Soviet forces invaded the country, ultimately starting the [Soviet–Afghan War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Afghan_War "Soviet–Afghan War").[^201] In May 1988, the [Soviets started to withdraw from Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_withdrawal_from_Afghanistan "Soviet withdrawal from Afghanistan"), due to international opposition, persistent anti-Soviet guerrilla warfare, and a lack of support by Soviet citizens.[^202]

#### Perestroika, democratisation and Russian sovereignty

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/President_Ronald_Reagan_Greets_a_Young_Boy_While_Touring_Red_Square_During_The_Moscow_Summit_in_The_USSR_-_DPLA_-_8f066efdc87eb23a889a89bd7c39173d.jpg/250px-President_Ronald_Reagan_Greets_a_Young_Boy_While_Touring_Red_Square_During_The_Moscow_Summit_in_The_USSR_-_DPLA_-_8f066efdc87eb23a889a89bd7c39173d.jpg)

Soviet leader Mikhail Gorbachev and US President Ronald Reagan in Red Square during the Moscow Summit, 31 May 1988

From 1985 onwards, the last Soviet leader [Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev"), who sought to enact liberal reforms in the Soviet system, introduced the policies of *[glasnost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glasnost "Glasnost")* (openness) and *[perestroika](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perestroika "Perestroika")* (restructuring) in an attempt to end the [period of economic stagnation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation "Era of Stagnation") and to [democratise the government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demokratizatsiya_\(Soviet_Union\) "Demokratizatsiya (Soviet Union)").[^203] This, however, led to the rise of strong nationalist and separatist movements across the country.[^204] Prior to 1991, the Soviet economy was the world's second-largest, but during its final years, it went into a crisis.[^205]

By 1991, economic and political turmoil began to boil over as the [Baltic states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_states "Baltic states") chose to secede from the Soviet Union.[^206] On 17 March, a [referendum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_Union_referendum "1991 Soviet Union referendum") was held, in which the vast majority of participating citizens voted in favour of changing the Soviet Union into a [renewed federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Union_Treaty "New Union Treaty").[^207] In June 1991, [Boris Yeltsin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin "Boris Yeltsin") became the first directly elected [President](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Russia "President of Russia") in Russian history when he was [elected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Russian_presidential_election "1991 Russian presidential election") President of the Russian SFSR.[^208] In August 1991, [a coup d'état attempt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt "1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt") by members of Gorbachev's government, directed against Gorbachev and aimed at preserving the Soviet Union, instead led to the end of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union.[^209] On 25 December 1991, following the [dissolution of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union"), along with contemporary Russia, fourteen other [post-Soviet states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-Soviet_states "Post-Soviet states") emerged.[^210]

### Independent Russian Federation

#### Transition to a market economy and political crises

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg/250px-Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg)

Vladimir Putin takes the oath of office as president on his first inauguration, with Boris Yeltsin looking over, 2000

The economic and political collapse of the Soviet Union led Russia into a deep and prolonged depression. During and after the disintegration of the Soviet Union, wide-ranging reforms including [privatisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privatization_in_Russia "Privatization in Russia") and [market and trade liberalisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_trade "Free trade") were undertaken, including radical changes along the lines of " [shock therapy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shock_therapy_\(economics\) "Shock therapy (economics)") ".[^211] The privatisation largely shifted control of enterprises from state agencies to individuals with inside connections in the government, which led to the rise of [Russian oligarchs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_oligarchs "Russian oligarchs").[^212] Many of the newly rich moved billions in cash and assets outside of the country in an enormous [capital flight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_flight "Capital flight").[^213] The depression of the economy led to the collapse of social services—the [birth rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birth_rate "Birth rate") plummeted while the [death rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_rate "Death rate") skyrocketed,[^214] [^215] and millions plunged into poverty,[^216] while extreme corruption,[^217] as well as criminal gangs and organised crime rose significantly.[^218]

In late 1993, tensions between Yeltsin and the Russian parliament culminated in [a constitutional crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993_Russian_constitutional_crisis "1993 Russian constitutional crisis") which ended violently through military force. During the crisis, Yeltsin was backed by Western governments, and over 100 people were killed.[^219]

#### Modern liberal constitution, international cooperation and economic stabilisation

In December, a [referendum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993_Russian_constitutional_referendum "1993 Russian constitutional referendum") was held and approved, which introduced a new constitution, giving the president enormous powers.[^220] The 1990s were plagued by armed conflicts in the [North Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Caucasus "North Caucasus"), both local ethnic skirmishes and separatist [Islamist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamist "Islamist") insurrections.[^221] From the time [Chechen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chechnya "Chechnya") separatists declared independence in the early 1990s, an [intermittent guerrilla war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Chechen_War "First Chechen War") was fought between the rebel groups and Russian forces.[^222] [Terrorist attacks against civilians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism_in_Russia "Terrorism in Russia") were carried out by Chechen separatists, claiming the lives of thousands of Russian civilians.[^6] [^223]

After the dissolution of the Soviet Union, Russia assumed responsibility for settling the latter's external debts.[^224] In 1992, most consumer price controls were eliminated, causing extreme inflation and significantly devaluing the rouble.[^225] High budget deficits coupled with increasing capital flight and inability to pay back debts, caused the [1998 Russian financial crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis "1998 Russian financial crisis"), which resulted in a further GDP decline.[^226]

#### Movement towards a modernised economy, political centralisation and democratic backsliding

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg/250px-Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg)

President Dmitry Medvedev with U.S. President Barack Obama after signing the New START treaty on nuclear disarmament in 2010, which was suspended by Putin in 2023 227

On 31 December 1999, President Yeltsin unexpectedly resigned,[^228] handing the post to the recently appointed prime minister and his chosen successor, [Vladimir Putin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin").[^229] Putin then won the [2000 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_Russian_presidential_election "2000 Russian presidential election"),[^230] and defeated the Chechen insurgency in the [Second Chechen War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Chechen_War "Second Chechen War").[^231]
