Putin won a [second presidential term](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Russian_presidential_election "2004 Russian presidential election") in 2004.[^232] [High oil prices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Price_of_petroleum "Price of petroleum") and a rise in foreign investment saw the [Russian economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_economy "Russian economy") and living standards improve significantly.[^233] Putin's rule increased stability, while transforming Russia into an [authoritarian state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarianism#Examples "Authoritarianism").[^234] In 2008, Putin took the post of prime minister, while [Dmitry Medvedev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev "Dmitry Medvedev") was [elected President](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Russian_presidential_election "2008 Russian presidential election") for one term, to hold onto power despite legal [term limits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Term_limit "Term limit");[^235] this period has been described as a " [tandemocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medvedev%E2%80%93Putin_tandemocracy "Medvedev–Putin tandemocracy") ".[^236]

Following a [diplomatic standoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Russo-Georgian_diplomatic_crisis "2008 Russo-Georgian diplomatic crisis") with neighbouring [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_\(country\) "Georgia (country)") in 2008, Russian forces [invaded the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War "Russo-Georgian War") from 1–16 August 2008 and [occupied territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupied_territories_of_Georgia "Occupied territories of Georgia") that it has [since considered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia "International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia") as independent states, [Abkhazia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abkhazia "Abkhazia") and [South Ossetia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Ossetia "South Ossetia").[^237] The conflict marked the [first war in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_conflicts_in_Europe "List of conflicts in Europe") in the 21st century.[^238] The [2008 constitutional amendments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Russia "2008 amendments to the Constitution of Russia") saw the terms of the president extend to six years and the lower house (State Duma) to five years.[^239] Putin then went on to win the [2012 presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Russian_presidential_election "2012 Russian presidential election"), which fuelled the " [Snow Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%932013_Russian_protests "2011–2013 Russian protests") " protests.[^240]

#### Russo-Ukrainian war and 2022 invasion

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg/330px-2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine.svg.png)

Map of Ukraine as of December 2025 Continuously controlled by Ukraine Currently occupied or controlled by Russia Formerly occupied by Russia

In 2014, following [a pro-Western revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolution_of_Dignity "Revolution of Dignity") in Ukraine, Russia invaded and [annexed Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation "Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation").[^241] [^242] It also supported [an insurgency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_pro-Russian_unrest_in_Ukraine "2014 pro-Russian unrest in Ukraine") in the [Donbas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donbas "Donbas") region of [eastern Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Ukraine "Eastern Ukraine"),[^243] and aided pro-Russian separatists waging a [war against the Ukrainian government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Donbas "War in Donbas").[^244] The [frozen conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frozen_conflict "Frozen conflict") [^245] escalated into [a full-scale Russian invasion of the remainder of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine") on 24 February 2022,[^246] [^247] initiating the largest [conventional war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conventional_warfare "Conventional warfare") in Europe since World War II.[^248] The invasion met with [international condemnation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reactions_to_the_2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Reactions to the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine"),[^249] and [expanded sanctions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "International sanctions during the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine") against Russia.[^250] Russia was expelled from the [Council of Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Council_of_Europe "Council of Europe") in March 2022,[^251] and [subsequently suspended](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_ES-11/3 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution ES-11/3") from the [United Nations Human Rights Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council "United Nations Human Rights Council") the following month.[^252]

Russia initially made rapid advances in the northern and eastern fronts, yet [failed to capture Kyiv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Kyiv_\(2022\) "Battle of Kyiv (2022)") and overthrow the Ukrainian government, leading to a subsequent [withdrawal from the north](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_front_of_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Northern front of the Russian invasion of Ukraine").[^253] [^254] In September 2022, Russia proclaimed the [annexation of four partially-occupied Ukrainian regions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annexation_of_southeastern_Ukraine_by_the_Russian_Federation "Annexation of southeastern Ukraine by the Russian Federation"), which was internationally [denounced as illegal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_ES-11/4 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution ES-11/4").[^255] Following the annexations, the conflict has settled into a [war of attrition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attrition_warfare "Attrition warfare") in the [southern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_front_of_the_Russo-Ukrainian_war_\(2022%E2%80%93present\) "Southern front of the Russo-Ukrainian war (2022–present)") and [eastern fronts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_front_of_the_Russo-Ukrainian_war_\(2022%E2%80%93present\) "Eastern front of the Russo-Ukrainian war (2022–present)"), with Russian forces making slow, limited advances and suffering [heavy casualties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casualties_of_the_Russo-Ukrainian_war "Casualties of the Russo-Ukrainian war").[^253] [^254] Russian forces have been [accused of committing war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crimes_in_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "War crimes in the Russian invasion of Ukraine") during the invasion,[^256] [^257] [^258] and occupied about a fifth of Ukraine's territory at the end of 2025.[^259]

## Geography

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Russian_Federation_Relief_Map.png/500px-Russian_Federation_Relief_Map.png)

Topographic map of Russia

Russia's vast landmass stretches over the easternmost part of Europe and the northernmost part of Asia.[^260] [^261] It spans the northernmost edge of [Eurasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia "Eurasia") and has the world's [fourth-longest coastline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_length_of_coastline "List of countries by length of coastline"), of over 37,653 km (23,396 mi).[^7] [^263] Russia lies between latitudes [41°](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/41st_parallel_north "41st parallel north") and [82° N](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/82nd_parallel_north "82nd parallel north"), and longitudes [19° E](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/19th_meridian_east "19th meridian east") and [169° W](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/169th_meridian_west "169th meridian west"), extending some 9,000 km (5,600 mi) east to west, and 2,500 to 4,000 km (1,600 to 2,500 mi) north to south.[^264] Russia, by landmass, is larger than three continents,[^8] and has the same surface area as [Pluto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluto "Pluto").[^265]

Russia has nine major mountain ranges, and they are found along the [southernmost regions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Russia "Southern Russia"), which share a significant portion of the [Caucasus Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains "Caucasus Mountains") (containing [Mount Elbrus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Elbrus "Mount Elbrus"), which at 5,642 m (18,510 ft) is the [highest peak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_elevation_extremes_by_region "List of elevation extremes by region") in Russia and Europe);[^19] the [Altai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altai_Mountains "Altai Mountains") and [Sayan Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sayan_Mountains "Sayan Mountains") in [Siberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberia "Siberia"); and in the [East Siberian Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Siberian_Mountains "East Siberian Mountains") and the [Kamchatka Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula "Kamchatka Peninsula") in the [Russian Far East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Far_East "Russian Far East") (containing [Klyuchevskaya Sopka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Klyuchevskaya_Sopka "Klyuchevskaya Sopka"), which at 4,750 m (15,584 ft) is the highest [active volcano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Active_volcano "Active volcano") in Eurasia).[^266] [^260] The [Ural Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ural_Mountains "Ural Mountains"), running north to south through the country's west, are rich in mineral resources, and form the [traditional boundary between Europe and Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boundary_between_Europe_and_Asia "Boundary between Europe and Asia").[^267] The [lowest point in Russia and Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_points_of_Europe#Elevation "Extreme points of Europe"), is situated at the head of the Caspian Sea, where the [Caspian Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Depression "Caspian Depression") reaches some 29 metres (95.1 ft) below sea level.[^268]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg/250px-Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg)

Frozen Lake Baikal near Olkhon Island, the third-largest lake island in the world

Russia, as one of the world's only three countries [bordering three oceans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_bordering_on_two_or_more_oceans "List of countries bordering on two or more oceans"),[^261] has links with a great number of seas.[^9] [^260] Its major islands and archipelagos include [Novaya Zemlya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya "Novaya Zemlya"), [Franz Josef Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land "Franz Josef Land"), [Severnaya Zemlya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Severnaya_Zemlya "Severnaya Zemlya"), the [New Siberian Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands "New Siberian Islands"), [Wrangel Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrangel_Island "Wrangel Island"), the [Kuril Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuril_Islands "Kuril Islands") (four of which are [disputed with Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuril_Islands_dispute "Kuril Islands dispute")), and [Sakhalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sakhalin "Sakhalin").[^269] [^270] The [Diomede Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diomede_Islands "Diomede Islands"), administered by Russia and the United States, are just 3.8 km (2.4 mi) apart;[^271] and [Kunashir Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kunashir_Island "Kunashir Island") of the Kuril Islands is merely 20 km (12.4 mi) from [Hokkaido](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hokkaido "Hokkaido"), Japan.[^14]

Russia has one of the world's largest surface water resources and is second only to Brazil by [total renewable water resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_total_renewable_water_resources "List of countries by total renewable water resources").[^272] Its lakes contain approximately one-quarter of the world's liquid [fresh water](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fresh_water "Fresh water").[^260] [Lake Baikal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Baikal "Lake Baikal"), the largest and most prominent among Russia's fresh water bodies, is the world's deepest, purest, oldest and most capacious fresh water lake, containing over one-fifth of the world's fresh surface water.[^273] [Ladoga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Ladoga "Lake Ladoga") and [Onega](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Onega "Lake Onega") in [northwestern Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwest_Russia "Northwest Russia") are two of the [largest lakes in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_lakes_of_Europe "List of largest lakes of Europe").[^261] Russia has over 100,000 rivers;[^261] the [Volga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga "Volga") in western Russia, which is widely regarded as the national river, is the [longest river](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Europe#Rivers_of_Europe_by_length "List of rivers of Europe") in Europe and forms the [Volga Delta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga_Delta "Volga Delta"), the largest [river delta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/River_delta "River delta") in the continent.[^274] The Siberian rivers of [Ob](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ob_River "Ob River"), [Yenisey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yenisey "Yenisey"), [Lena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lena_River "Lena River"), and [Amur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amur_River "Amur River") are among the world's [longest rivers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_length "List of rivers by length").[^275]

### Climate

The size of Russia and the remoteness of many of its areas from the sea result in the dominance of the [humid continental climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate") throughout most of the country, except for the tundra and the extreme southwest. Mountain ranges in the south and east obstruct the flow of warm air masses from the [Indian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Ocean "Indian Ocean") and Pacific oceans, while the [European Plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Plain "European Plain") spanning its west and north opens it to influence from the Atlantic and Arctic oceans.[^260] Most of northwest Russia and Siberia have a [subarctic climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subarctic_climate "Subarctic climate"), with extremely severe winters in the inner regions of northeast Siberia (mostly [Sakha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sakha_Republic "Sakha Republic"), where the Northern [Pole of Cold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pole_of_Cold "Pole of Cold") is located with the record low temperature of −71.2 °C or −96.2 °F),[^269] and more moderate winters elsewhere. Russia's vast coastline along the Arctic Ocean and the [Russian Arctic islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Arctic_islands "Russian Arctic islands") have a [polar climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_climate "Polar climate").[^260]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/500px-Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png)

Köppen climate classification of Russia

The coastal part of [Krasnodar Krai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krasnodar_Krai "Krasnodar Krai") on the Black Sea, most notably [Sochi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sochi "Sochi"), and some coastal and interior strips of the [North Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Caucasus "North Caucasus") possess a [humid subtropical climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate "Humid subtropical climate") with mild and wet winters.[^260] In many regions of East Siberia and the Russian Far East, winter is dry compared to summer, while other parts of the country experience more even precipitation across seasons. Winter precipitation in most parts of the country usually falls as snow. The westernmost parts of Kaliningrad Oblast and some parts in the south of Krasnodar Krai and the North Caucasus have an [oceanic climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceanic_climate "Oceanic climate").[^260] The region along the Lower Volga and Caspian Sea coast, as well as some southernmost slivers of Siberia, possess a [semi-arid climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-arid_climate "Semi-arid climate").[^276]

Throughout much of the territory, there are only two distinct seasons, winter and summer, as spring and autumn are usually brief.[^260] The coldest month is January (February on the coastline); the warmest is usually July. Great ranges of temperature are typical. In winter, temperatures get colder both from south to north and from west to east. Summers can be quite hot, even in Siberia.[^277] [Climate change in Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_Russia "Climate change in Russia") is causing more frequent [wildfires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wildfires_in_Russia "Wildfires in Russia"),[^278] and thawing the country's large expanse of [permafrost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permafrost "Permafrost").[^279]

### Biodiversity

Russia, owing to its gigantic size, has diverse ecosystems, including [polar deserts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_desert "Polar desert"), [tundra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tundra "Tundra"), [forest-tundra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest-tundra "Forest-tundra"), [taiga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiga "Taiga"), [mixed and broadleaf forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_and_mixed_forests "Temperate broadleaf and mixed forests"), [forest steppe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest_steppe "Forest steppe"), [steppe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steppe "Steppe"), semi-desert, and [subtropics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subtropics "Subtropics").[^280] About half of Russia's territory is forested,[^19] and it has the world's largest area of forest.[^281]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%85%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82.jpg/250px-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%85%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%B5%D1%82.jpg)

Yugyd Va National Park in the Komi Republic is the largest national park in Europe. 267

Russian biodiversity includes 12,500 species of [vascular plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vascular_plant "Vascular plant"), 2,200 species of [bryophytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bryophyte "Bryophyte"), about 3,000 species of [lichens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lichen "Lichen"), 7,000–9,000 species of [algae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algae "Algae"), and 20,000–25,000 species of fungi. Russian [fauna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fauna "Fauna") is composed of [320 species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Russia "List of mammals of Russia") of [mammals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammals "Mammals"), over [732 species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Russia "List of birds of Russia") of birds, 75 species of reptiles, about 30 species of [amphibians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphibian "Amphibian"), [343 species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_freshwater_fish_of_Russia "List of freshwater fish of Russia") of [freshwater fish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freshwater_fish "Freshwater fish") (high [endemism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemism "Endemism")), approximately 1,500 species of [saltwater fishes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saltwater_fish "Saltwater fish"), 9 species of [cyclostomata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyclostomata "Cyclostomata"), and approximately 100–150,000 [invertebrates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invertebrate "Invertebrate") (high endemism).[^280] [^282] Approximately 1,100 rare and endangered plant and animal species are included in the [Russian Red Data Book](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Data_Book_of_the_Russian_Federation "Red Data Book of the Russian Federation").[^280]

Russia's entirely natural ecosystems are conserved in nearly 15,000 specially protected natural territories of various statuses, occupying more than 10% of the country's total area.[^280] They include 45 [biosphere reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosphere_reserve "Biosphere reserve"),[^283] 64 [national parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_parks_of_Russia "National parks of Russia"), and 101 [nature reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zapovednik "Zapovednik").[^284] Although in decline, the country still has many ecosystems which are still considered [intact forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intact_forest_landscape "Intact forest landscape"), mainly in the northern taiga areas, and the subarctic tundra of Siberia.[^285] Russia had a [Forest Landscape Integrity Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index "Forest Landscape Integrity Index") mean score of 9.02 in 2019, ranking 10th out of 172 countries, and the first ranked major nation globally.[^286]

[^1]: [Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimea "Crimea"), which was [annexed by Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation "Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation") in 2014, remains [internationally recognised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262") as a part of Ukraine.[^13] Donetsk, Luhansk, Kherson, and Zaporizhzhia oblasts, which were [annexed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_annexation_of_Donetsk,_Kherson,_Luhansk_and_Zaporizhzhia_oblasts "Russian annexation of Donetsk, Kherson, Luhansk and Zaporizhzhia oblasts") —though are only partially occupied—in 2022, also remain [internationally recognised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_ES-11/4 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution ES-11/4") as a part of Ukraine. The southernmost [Kuril Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuril_Islands "Kuril Islands") have been the subject of a [territorial dispute](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuril_Islands_dispute "Kuril Islands dispute") with Japan since their occupation by the Soviet Union at the end of World War II.[^14]

[^2]: [Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language"): Россия, [romanised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian "Romanization of Russian"): *Rossiya*, [\[rɐˈsʲijə\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian "Help:IPA/Russian")

[^3]: [Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language"): Российская Федерация, [romanised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian "Romanization of Russian"): *Rossiyskaya Federatsiya*, IPA: [\[rɐˈsʲijskəjə fʲɪdʲɪˈratsɨjə\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian "Help:IPA/Russian")

[^4]: The names 'Russia' and the 'Russian Federation' are declared by the constitution to be co-equal.[^29]

[^5]: The fourteen countries bordering Russia are [^30] [Norway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norway "Norway") and [Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finland "Finland") to the northwest; [Estonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estonia "Estonia"), [Latvia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latvia "Latvia"), [Belarus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belarus "Belarus") and [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine") to the west, as well as [Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithuania "Lithuania") and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland "Poland") (with [Kaliningrad Oblast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaliningrad_Oblast "Kaliningrad Oblast")); [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_\(country\) "Georgia (country)") and [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") to the southwest; [Kazakhstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan") and [Mongolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongolia "Mongolia") to the south; [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China") and [North Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea") to the southeast. Russia also shares [maritime boundaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maritime_boundary "Maritime boundary") with Japan and the United States, as well as borders with the two [partially recognised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partially_recognized_states "Partially recognized states") breakaway states of [South Ossetia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Ossetia "South Ossetia") and [Abkhazia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abkhazia "Abkhazia") that it occupies in Georgia.

[^6]: Most notably the [Budyonnovsk hospital hostage crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budyonnovsk_hospital_hostage_crisis "Budyonnovsk hospital hostage crisis"), the [Russian apartment bombings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_apartment_bombings "Russian apartment bombings"), the [Moscow theatre hostage crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow_theater_hostage_crisis "Moscow theater hostage crisis"), and the [Beslan school siege](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beslan_school_siege "Beslan school siege")

[^7]: Russia has an additional 850 km (530 mi) of coastline along the [Caspian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caspian_Sea "Caspian Sea"), which is the world's largest inland body of water, and has been variously classified as a sea or a lake.[^262]

[^8]: Russia, by land area, is larger than the continents of [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia_\(continent\) "Australia (continent)"), [Antarctica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctica "Antarctica"), and Europe, although it covers a large part of the latter itself. Its land area could be roughly compared to that of South America.

[^9]: Russia borders, clockwise, to its southwest: the [Black Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Sea "Black Sea") and the [Sea of Azov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Azov "Sea of Azov"), to its west: the [Baltic Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea"), to its north: the [Barents Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barents_Sea "Barents Sea") ([White Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Sea "White Sea"), [Pechora Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pechora_Sea "Pechora Sea")), the [Kara Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kara_Sea "Kara Sea"), the [Laptev Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laptev_Sea "Laptev Sea"), and the [East Siberian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Siberian_Sea "East Siberian Sea"), to its northeast: the [Chukchi Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chukchi_Sea "Chukchi Sea") and the [Bering Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bering_Sea "Bering Sea"), and to its southeast: the [Sea of Okhotsk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk "Sea of Okhotsk") and the [Sea of Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Japan "Sea of Japan").

[^10]: In 2020, [constitutional amendments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Russia "2020 amendments to the Constitution of Russia") were signed into law that limit the president to two terms overall rather than two consecutive terms, with this limit reset for current and previous presidents.[^294]

[^11]: Including bodies on territory disputed between Russia and Ukraine whose annexation has not been internationally recognised: the [Republic of Crimea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea_\(Russia\) "Republic of Crimea (Russia)") and the federal city of [Sevastopol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sevastopol "Sevastopol") since the annexation of Crimea in 2014,[^13] and territories set up following the [Russian annexation of Donetsk, Kherson, Luhansk and Zaporizhzhia oblasts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_annexation_of_Donetsk,_Kherson,_Luhansk_and_Zaporizhzhia_oblasts "Russian annexation of Donetsk, Kherson, Luhansk and Zaporizhzhia oblasts") in 2022.

[^12]: The Sreda Arena Atlas 2012 did not count the populations of two federal subjects of Russia where the majority of the population is Muslim, namely [Chechnya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chechnya "Chechnya") and [Ingushetia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ingushetia "Ingushetia"), which together had a population of nearly 2 million, thus the proportion of Muslims was possibly slightly underestimated.[^576]

Ivan's statecraft was the great prototype, a classic Russian system of absolutism and militarism under cautious and scrupulous control... Ivan III laid the foundations of Russian absolutism... In a serious break with tradition, Russia entered the constitutional era... Russian autocracy came to an end, and the Revolution of 1905 soon withered and died—not, however, without fateful consequences.
